## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics / materials science (thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which is the standard setting for constitutive laws in solids where elastic modulus, yield stress, and hardening/softening behavior depend on temperature. Likely relationships include thermoelasticity (E(T)), thermal expansion shifting the mechanical strain, and temperature-dependent plastic flow/hardening.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear thermoelastic (Hooke with temperature-dependent modulus): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (small-strain elasticity with stiffness varying with T)
- Exponential stiffness softening with temperature: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (empirical E(T) dependence over moderate T ranges)
- Thermal strain shift (1D thermoelastic): sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1 * T) (stress depends on mechanical strain epsilon - alpha*T, expressed as epsilon + c1*T)
- Polynomial modulus model: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (engineering fit for E(T) in limited temperature windows)
- Piecewise elastic–plastic idealization (yield with temperature): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (epsilon - c2) + c3 * tanh(c4 * (epsilon - c2)) (smooth approximation to yielding/transition near a yield strain)
- Ramberg–Osgood (implicit structure, explicit surrogate): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * Abs(epsilon)**c2 * Sign(epsilon) (captures nonlinear elastic/plastic-like curvature in σ–ε)
- Ludwik–Hollomon hardening with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + c2 * Abs(epsilon)**c3 (strain hardening offset by temperature dependence of strength)
- Voce hardening (saturating stress) with T-dependent saturation: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + (c2 + c3 * T) * (1 - exp(-c4 * Abs(epsilon))) * Sign(epsilon) (hardening that approaches a saturation level)
- Exponential strain softening (damage/necking proxy): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon * exp(-c2 * Abs(epsilon)) (stress rises then drops at large strain)
- Hyperelastic polynomial (1D surrogate): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**3 (nonlinear elasticity with temperature-dependent coefficients)
- Brittle–ductile/phase-transition blending: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + c2 * tanh(c3 * (T - c4)) * epsilon (smooth change in stiffness/response near a transition temperature)
- Coupled invariants-like scaling (dimensionless-style): sigma = c0 * (c1 * T + 1) * (c2 * Abs(epsilon) + 1)**c3 * Sign(epsilon) (multiplicative coupling of thermal factor and strain nonlinearity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Small-strain elastic regime → sigma proportional to epsilon, with proportionality E(T) that is often decreasing with T (use (c0 + c1*T)*epsilon or c0*exp(c1*T)*epsilon).
- Thermal expansion / residual stress effects → sigma depends on an effective strain (epsilon + c*T), giving nonzero stress at epsilon = 0 if constrained.
- Yield/transition behavior → a sharp change in slope around a characteristic strain can be approximated smoothly with tanh(c*(epsilon-c0)) added to a linear term.
- Strain hardening (work hardening) → monotone concave increase often fits power laws in |epsilon| (Abs(epsilon)**c) added to a base strength that depends on T.
- Saturating hardening at large strain → use (1 - exp(-c*|epsilon|)) to approach an asymptote (Voce-type behavior).
- Thermal softening of strength/hardening → make yield/flow parameters linear or exponential in T, e.g., (c0 + c1*T) multiplying or shifting hardening terms.
- Post-peak softening/damage → include an exp(-c*|epsilon|) factor multiplying an otherwise increasing law to produce a peak then decline.
- Symmetry under tension/compression in 1D idealization → sigma often odd in epsilon; enforce with Sign(epsilon) and Abs(epsilon) in nonlinear terms.

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (MatSci6)
============================================================
GT: c0*epsilon*(-c1*(T - c2) + c3) + epsilon*c4*(T - c5)**c6
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed) simplifies structurally to
\[
\text{GT}=\epsilon\Big(21.69809045\big(-0.0546033494\,(T-342.5784399)+1\big)+5.649723021\,(T-342.5784399)^2\Big).
\]
So GT is **(i)** linear in \(\epsilon\) (overall factor \(\epsilon\)), **(ii)** a **quadratic polynomial in \(T\)** (after expanding \((T-342.5784)^2\)), and **(iii)** contains **no** \(\exp,\sin,\log,|\cdot|\), and **no** \(\epsilon^3\) terms. Also \(\text{GT}(0,T)=0\) for all \(T\).

A candidate can only match if, by choosing its constants (and possibly restricting to a plausible continuous domain), it can be made exactly \(\epsilon\cdot(\text{quadratic in }T)\) with no other \(\epsilon\)-dependence.

---

### Candidates 1–9
All of 1–9 have a leading term \(T^2 c0\) **not multiplied by \(\epsilon\)**. Since GT has no \(\epsilon^0\) term, we must set \(c0=0\). They also have \(T\cdot c1\exp(c2|\epsilon|)\) which cannot become \(\epsilon\cdot(\text{poly in }T)\) on any open domain:  
- If \(c1\neq 0\), \(\exp(c2|\epsilon|)\) is not proportional to \(\epsilon\) on any interval.  
- So set \(c1=0\).  
They also include \(c5\exp(c6\sin(\cdot))\) (an \(\epsilon\)-dependent non-polynomial term) unless \(c5=0\). Set \(c5=0\).  
Then remaining terms are combinations of \(T\), constants, \(\epsilon\), \(\epsilon^3\), etc. GT needs \(\epsilon\cdot(\text{quadratic in }T)\), i.e., it needs terms like \(\epsilon T^2, \epsilon T, \epsilon\). None of 1–9 can produce an \(\epsilon T^2\) term because their \(T^2\) term is independent of \(\epsilon\) and can only be removed, not converted. Also many have unavoidable \(T\) (candidate 1,2,4,7,8,9 include “+T”) which cannot be removed unless its coefficient is parameterized (it is not). Therefore 1–9 cannot match.

### Candidates 10–13, 16, 25, 30, 40
These have \(T^2 c0\) (must set \(c0=0\)) and \(T c1\exp(c2|\epsilon|)\) (must set \(c1=0\)), plus various \(T c3\) or \(T c3\epsilon^3\), \(T c4\epsilon^3\), constants, \(\exp(\sin(\cdot))\), \(\epsilon^3\), \(T^{-5}\), etc. After zeroing all non-polynomial/nonlinear-in-\(\epsilon\) parts (setting the relevant coefficients to 0), what remains is at best a linear function of \(T\) plus possibly \(\epsilon^3\) terms. None can generate \(\epsilon T^2\) or \(\epsilon T\) simultaneously with \(\epsilon\) factorization; they either have no \(\epsilon\) factor at all in the \(T\)-polynomial part, or only \(\epsilon^3\) coupling. So they cannot match GT.

### Candidates 14, 17, 18, 21, 41
Contain \(\log(\cdot)\) terms. GT has no logarithms. The only way is to set the log coefficient to 0 (e.g., \(c4=0\)). After doing so, these reduce to the same structural issues as above: no way to create \(\epsilon\cdot(\text{quadratic in }T)\) because there is no \(\epsilon T^2\) term available. So no match.

### Candidates 15, 20, 23, 38
Contain extra exponentials in \(\epsilon\) or \(T\) (e.g., \(c4\exp(c5\epsilon)\), \(c4\exp(Tc5)\)). To match GT, those coefficients must be 0. Then again the remaining polynomial-in-\(T\) part is not multiplied by \(\epsilon\) (and/or includes an unavoidable “+T” in some), and there is still no mechanism to produce \(\epsilon T^2\). No match.

### Candidates 19, 22, 24, 26–29, 31–37, 39, 42–50
These include various combinations of:
- unavoidable \(T^2 c0\) (must be zeroed),
- unavoidable \(T c1\exp(c2|\epsilon|)\) (must be zeroed),
- \(\exp(\sin(\cdot))\) (must be zeroed),
- \(\epsilon^3\) or \(T\epsilon^3\) couplings (GT needs linear \(\epsilon\), not cubic),
- sometimes an unavoidable “+T” (cannot be removed),
- sometimes \(T^{-5}\) (cannot be made into a polynomial; must be zeroed but it has fixed coefficient 1 in those candidates, so impossible).

Key blockers among these:
- **No candidate has any term of the form \(\epsilon T^2\)** or \(\epsilon (T-\text{shift})^2\). The only \(T^2\) term is always \(T^2 c0\) without \(\epsilon\). Setting \(c0=0\) removes it, leaving no quadratic-in-\(T\) dependence at all (except via non-polynomial functions like log/exp which must also be removed to match GT).
- Many candidates have fixed “+T” or fixed \(T^{-5}\) terms. GT has neither; fixed terms cannot be eliminated by parameter choice.
- Trig phase-shift considerations are irrelevant here because GT has no trig terms; the only way to match is to zero out trig/exponential parts, which then leaves the missing \(\epsilon T^2\) structure.

Thus none of 19, 22, 24, 26–29, 31–37, 39, 42–50 can be made identical to GT on any plausible continuous domain.

---

### Conditional equivalence check
Could restricting the domain (e.g., \(\epsilon=0\) or \(T=\text{const}\)) help? The rules require a “plausible continuous domain condition” like inequalities, not collapsing to a single point or forcing \(\epsilon\equiv 0\). Any open interval in \(\epsilon\) will still expose that candidates either:
- have nonzero \(\epsilon^0\) terms in \(T\) (unless forced to zero), and/or
- lack the required \(\epsilon T^2\) term entirely.

So conditional equivalence does not rescue any candidate.

---

Final verdict: none of the candidates can be parameter-tuned to equal \(\epsilon\) times a quadratic polynomial in \(T\) as in the GT.

[NO MATCH]

Conclusion: No match

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT numerical expression is:
```
21.698090453033654*epsilon*(-0.05460334940892902*(T - 342.5784399345082) + 1) + epsilon*5.6497230214391285*(T - 342.5784399345082)**2
```

Let me expand this:

First term: `21.698090453033654*epsilon*(-0.05460334940892902*T + 0.05460334940892902*342.578... + 1)`
= `21.698090453033654*epsilon*(-0.05460334940892902*T + 18.7058... + 1)`
= `21.698090453033654*epsilon*(-0.05460334940892902*T + 19.7058...)`
= `-1.18488...*epsilon*T + 427.81...*epsilon`

Second term: `5.6497230214391285*epsilon*(T - 342.578...)^2`
= `5.6497230214391285*epsilon*(T^2 - 685.157...*T + 117359.97...)`
= `5.6497230214391285*epsilon*T^2 - 3871.06...*epsilon*T + 662893...*epsilon`

Combining all terms:
= `5.6497...*epsilon*T^2 + (-1.1849... - 3871.06...)*epsilon*T + (427.81... + 662893...)*epsilon`
= `5.6497...*epsilon*T^2 - 3872.25...*epsilon*T + 663321...*epsilon`

So GT = **epsilon * (a*T² + b*T + c)** where a, b, c are specific constants.

This is a polynomial in epsilon and T with the structure:
**GT = A·epsilon·T² + B·epsilon·T + C·epsilon**

The basis functions are: `epsilon*T²`, `epsilon*T`, and `epsilon`.

## Candidate Analysis

All candidates contain terms like:
- `T²*c0` (pure T², no epsilon)
- `T*c1*exp(c2*|epsilon|)` (exponential in epsilon)
- `T*c3*epsilon³` (cubic in epsilon)
- Various other terms with exp, sin, log, etc.

The GT requires `epsilon*T²`, but candidates have `T²*c0` (no epsilon factor). These are different basis functions - `T²` vs `epsilon*T²` are linearly independent.

Even if we set c0=0 to eliminate the `T²*c0` term, none of the candidates contain an `epsilon*T²` term. Let me check each candidate carefully for any term that could produce `epsilon*T²`.

Looking through all 50 candidates, the available term types are:
- `T²*c0` — gives T² (no epsilon)
- `T*exp(|epsilon|)` — not polynomial in epsilon
- `T*epsilon³` — gives T*epsilon³
- `T*epsilon` — gives T*epsilon (some candidates)
- `T` — gives T
- `exp(sin(...))` — transcendental
- `epsilon³`, `epsilon` — pure epsilon terms
- `log(...)` — transcendental
- `T*epsilon³` with coefficient 1 (some candidates)
- `T^c4` — power of T

**None of the candidates contain an `epsilon*T²` term.** The GT fundamentally requires this basis function. The `T²*c0` term in candidates is `T²` without epsilon, which is linearly independent from `epsilon*T²`. Setting c0 to any value cannot produce `epsilon*T²`.

No candidate can match the GT because the essential basis function `epsilon*T²` is absent from all candidates.

Let me verify: Could `T*c1*exp(c2*|epsilon|)` somehow produce `epsilon*T²`? No — it's linear in T and exponential in epsilon, not quadratic in T.
